This handler is either the view wrapper or the next middleware in the chain, creating a functional composition pattern.\\n\\n4. **Async/sync adaptation** (lines 50-61): Django detects whether middleware supports synchronous and/or asynchronous requests via `sync_capable` and `async_capable` attributes and adapts the handler accordingly.\\n\\n5. **Exception wrapping** (lines 39, 97): Each middleware is wrapped with `convert_exception_to_response()` to ensure exceptions are converted to HTTP responses before passing to the next middleware.\\n\\n### Request/Response Processing Order\\n\\nThe middleware processing order follows the \\\"onion\\\" pattern documented in `docs/topics/http/middleware.txt` (lines 135-151):\\n\\n**Request phase (top-down):**\\nRequests pass through middleware in the order defined in `settings.MIDDLEWARE`, from top to bottom. This is enforced through the nested callable structure created during initialization.\\n\\n**Response phase (bottom-up):**\\nResponses return through middleware in reverse order - only through the middleware layers that the request actually passed through. This is implemented via the nested callable chain: when middleware calls `get_response()` and receives a response, it processes that response before returning it.\\n\\n### Middleware Hook Methods\\n\\nThe `MiddlewareMixin` class in `django/utils/deprecation.py` (lines 275-331) provides the standard interface for middleware:\\n\\n1. **`__init__(get_response)`** (lines 279-290): Called once when the server starts, receives the next callable in the chain.\\n\\n2. **`__call__(request)`** (lines 302-312): Invokes in this order for synchronous requests:\\n   - Calls `process_request()` if defined\\n   - Calls `get_response(request)` to invoke the next middleware/view\\n   - Calls `process_response()` if defined\\n   - Returns the response\\n\\n3. **`__acall__(request)`** (lines 314-331): Async version with identical semantics but using `await` and `sync_to_async` adaptation.\\n\\n### View, Exception, and Template Response Middleware\\n\\nThe `_get_response()` and `_get_response_async()` methods (lines 176-228 and 230-300 in base.py) handle special middleware hooks:\\n\\n- **View middleware** (line 79-83): Collected in reverse order, executed in forward order just before the view\\n- **Template response middleware** (lines 84-89, 211-220): Applied after the view returns if the response has a render method\\n- **Exception middleware** (lines 90-95, 363-366): Called when exceptions occur, executed in reverse order\\n\\n### Exception Handling\\n\\nThe `convert_exception_to_response()` function in `django/core/handlers/exception.py` (lines 25-61) is a critical component. It wraps each middleware with exception handling that converts exceptions to HTTP responses, preventing middleware from leaking exceptions and ensuring each middleware can rely on receiving responses rather than exceptions.\\n\\n### Comparison with WSGI Middleware\\n\\nDjango's MIDDLEWARE differs fundamentally from traditional WSGI middleware:\\n\\n1. **WSGI pattern**: Traditional WSGI middleware wraps an application returning an iterator, using the nested callable pattern but operating at the HTTP request/response level with different semantics.\\n\\n2. **Django pattern**: Django middleware uses a factory function/class taking a callable (`get_response`) and returning a middleware callable. The middleware is responsible for calling `get_response()` to proceed, creating a more explicit control flow.\\n\\n3. **Short-circuiting behavior** (lines 148-151 in middleware.txt): Django's middleware can return a response without calling `get_response()`, which prevents inner middleware from seeing the request/response. This is different from WSGI where all middleware typically see all requests.\\n\\n4. **Exception handling**: Django's middleware have explicit exception handling via `process_exception()` hooks that run in reverse order, whereas WSGI relies on exception propagation.\\n\\n5. **Special hooks**: Django provides `process_view()`, `process_template_response()`, and `process_exception()` as special hooks beyond the basic request/response cycle, enabling more granular control over request processing phases.\\n\\n### Handler Integration\\n\\nThe concrete implementations in `django/core/handlers/wsgi.py` (lines 113-144) and `django/core/handlers/asgi.py` (lines 143-152) show how the middleware system is initialized and used:\\n\\n- **WSGIHandler.__init__** calls `self.load_middleware()` during instantiation\\n- **ASGIHandler.__init__** calls `self.load_middleware(is_async=True)` for async context\\n- Both handlers call `get_response()` (lines 124 in wsgi.py, 224 in asgi.py) which invokes the constructed `_middleware_chain`\\n\\nThis design ensures Django's middleware system provides a robust, layered architecture for request/response processing with proper exception handling, async support, and explicit control flow through the callable chain.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
